  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>With the finalized abstraction of the Mahout DSL plans from the backend operations (<a href="https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/MAHOUT-1529" title="Finalize abstraction of distributed logical plans from backend operations" class="issue-link" data-issue-key="MAHOUT-1529"><del>MAHOUT-1529</del></a>), it should be possible to integrate further backends for the Mahout DSL. Apache Flink would be a suitable candidate to act as a good execution backend. </p> 
                  <p>With respect to the implementation, the biggest difference between Spark and Flink at the moment is probably the incremental rollout of plans, which is triggered by Spark's actions and which is not supported by Flink yet. However, the Flink community is working on this issue. For the moment, it should be possible to circumvent this problem by writing intermediate results required by an action to HDFS and reading from there.</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

matrix(idx, ::) := vec }\\n\u003cp\u003e              out.collect((keys.toArray(classTag), matrix))\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n            } else \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n{\\n              val matrix = new SparseRowMatrix(vectors.size, ncolLocal, vectors.toArray)\\n              out.collect((keys.toArray(classTag), matrix))\\n            }\\n\u003cp\u003e          }\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n        }\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n      })\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e      new BlockifiedFlinkDrm(parts, ncol)\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    }\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    ```\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    a comment from @dlyubimov on this partitioning issue:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt;\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; apparently flink plans (product splitting) may produce empty partitions. Spark physical operators were careful to avoid this when deciding on the product parallelism, so with Spark this is not known to happen (neither with h20 for that matter). \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt;\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; Technically of course the codes must survive empty partition situations. However, it has been patched only on a need-to-do basis, so obviously there are spots like blockify() that are not really fixed yet out of mere necessity. Since like i said the spark optimizer is careful to avoid this, it apparently never happened before (and i ran a lot of spark code on this). \u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt;\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; So... of course we should patch the blockify code. However, the real problem IMO is the careful review of the splitting logic in Flink physical layer. Empty splits generally should not happen more often than is absolutely unavoidable (especially if this happens after drmParallelize that explicitly said to make 2 partitions out of 500-odd rows, give or take).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"githubbot\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14964012_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=githubbot\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"githubbot\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e ASF GitHub Bot\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14964012_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'19\\/Oct\\/15 20:38\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-10-19T20:38:13+0000\'\u003e19\\/Oct\\/15 20:38\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Github user andrewpalumbo commented on the pull request: \\n\\n      https:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/137#issuecomment-149339970  \\n\\n     I looked at this briefly last night, was able to get it down to only 2 failing tests (of 6 total) in the DistributedDecompositionSuite: dspca and dals. \\n\\n     It looks like `FlinkDrm.blockify()` is creating or adding at least one empty partition to the `BlockifiedFlinkDrm &#91;K&#93; ` (possibly some idiosyncrasy with the backing flink Dataset..?  just a quick guess). \\n\\n     It\'s probably something deeper than that causing the problems, but by adding the below check for an empty partition, all DSSVD tests pass. \\n\\n     The DSPCA test runs without exception but fails with an incorrect finishing value.  The DALS test runs out of heap space even with -Xmx4g set. \\n\\n     FlinkDrm.scala: \\n    ``` \\n    def blockify(): BlockifiedFlinkDrm &#91;K&#93;  = { \\n      val ncolLocal = ncol \\n      val classTag = implicitly[ClassTag &#91;K&#93; ] \\n\\n       val parts = ds.mapPartition(new MapPartitionFunction[DrmTuple &#91;K&#93; , (Array &#91;K&#93; , Matrix)] { \\n        def mapPartition(values: Iterable[DrmTuple &#91;K&#93; ], out: Collector[(Array &#91;K&#93; , Matrix)]): Unit = { \\n          val it = values.asScala.seq \\n            val (keys, vectors) = it.unzip \\n\\n             if (!(vectors.isEmpty)) { \\/\\/ &lt;-- adding this check makes DSSVD tests pass \\n\\n             val isDense = vectors.head.isDense \\n\\n             if (isDense) { \\n              val matrix = new DenseMatrix(vectors.size, ncolLocal) \\n              vectors.zipWithIndex.foreach  \\n{ case (vec, idx) =&gt; matrix(idx, ::) := vec }\\n               out.collect((keys.toArray(classTag), matrix)) \\n            } else  \\n{\\n              val matrix = new SparseRowMatrix(vectors.size, ncolLocal, vectors.toArray)\\n              out.collect((keys.toArray(classTag), matrix))\\n            }\\n           } \\n        } \\n      }) \\n\\n       new BlockifiedFlinkDrm(parts, ncol) \\n    } \\n    ``` \\n\\n     a comment from @dlyubimov on this partitioning issue: \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; apparently flink plans (product splitting) may produce empty partitions. Spark physical operators were careful to avoid this when deciding on the product parallelism, so with Spark this is not known to happen (neither with h20 for that matter).  \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; Technically of course the codes must survive empty partition situations. However, it has been patched only on a need-to-do basis, so obviously there are spots like blockify() that are not really fixed yet out of mere necessity. Since like i said the spark optimizer is careful to avoid this, it apparently never happened before (and i ran a lot of spark code on this).  \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; So... of course we should patch the blockify code. However, the real problem IMO is the careful review of the splitting logic in Flink physical layer. Empty splits generally should not happen more often than is absolutely unavoidable (especially if this happens after drmParallelize that explicitly said to make 2 partitions out of 500-odd rows, give or take). \\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-14964566\\\" class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-10-21T12:48:41+0000\'\u003e21\\/Oct\\/15 12:48\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eGithub user tillrohrmann commented on the pull request:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/161#issuecomment-149884474\\\" class=\\\"external-link\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\u003ehttps:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/161#issuecomment-149884474\u003c\\/a\u003e\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    The problem of the `OutOfMemoryError` in `dals` of the `DistributedDecompositionSuite` is the following: \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    In order parallelize the input matrix, the `FlinkEngine` creates a `Collection[DrmTuple\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;Int&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e]` which is given to Flink\'s `CollectionInputFormat`. The `CollectionInputFormat` is simply a wrapper for a collection which is serialized and shipped to the corresponding data source at runtime. The problem is that the matrix rows in the collection of `DrmTuple\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;Int&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e` are of type `MatrixVectorView`. Instances of this class hold a reference to the original matrix. Therefore, serializing an instance of `MatrixVectorView` effectively boils down to serializing the complete input matrix for each row. This means that the `CollectionInputFormat` needs memory of order `size(inputMatrix) * rows(inputMatrix)` to serialize the given collection of `DrmTuple\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;Int&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e` instances.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    The input size for the dals test case are `500 * 500`. This means that the input matrix has roughly the size of 2 MB. The serialized `CollectionInputFormat` has then a size of roughly 1 GB, because we serialize the matrix for each row. If you replace `FlinkEngine.scala:231` with `val rows = (0 until m.nrow).map(i =&gt; (i, dvec(m(i, :\u003cimg class=\\\"emoticon\\\" src=\\\"\\/jira\\/images\\/icons\\/emoticons\\/smile.png\\\" height=\\\"16\\\" width=\\\"16\\\" align=\\\"absmiddle\\\" alt=\\\"\\\" border=\\\"0\\\"\\/\u003e).asInstanceOf\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;Vector&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e))`, the test will pass the serialization point (but fail with another error \u003cimg class=\\\"emoticon\\\" src=\\\"\\/jira\\/images\\/icons\\/emoticons\\/sad.png\\\" height=\\\"16\\\" width=\\\"16\\\" align=\\\"absmiddle\\\" alt=\\\"\\\" border=\\\"0\\\"\\/\u003e The reason why 1 GB of memory, given that you set the max limit to 4 GB, is already enough to crash Flink is that Flink reserver per default 70% of the available memory for its managed memory (for sorting and hashing).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    I think it would make sense to convert possible `Views` to its materialized form before distributing the data in the cluster. That way, you avoid the creation of unnecessary data which might be ok for the local use case where the data is shared.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    I hope this sheds a little bit of light in the `OutOfMemoryError` you\'ve encountered. \u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"githubbot\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14966755_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=githubbot\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"githubbot\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e ASF GitHub Bot\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14966755_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'21\\/Oct\\/15 12:48\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-10-21T12:48:41+0000\'\u003e21\\/Oct\\/15 12:48\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Github user tillrohrmann commented on the pull request: \\n\\n      https:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/161#issuecomment-149884474  \\n\\n     The problem of the `OutOfMemoryError` in `dals` of the `DistributedDecompositionSuite` is the following:  \\n\\n     In order parallelize the input matrix, the `FlinkEngine` creates a `Collection[DrmTuple &#91;Int&#93; ]` which is given to Flink\'s `CollectionInputFormat`. The `CollectionInputFormat` is simply a wrapper for a collection which is serialized and shipped to the corresponding data source at runtime. The problem is that the matrix rows in the collection of `DrmTuple &#91;Int&#93; ` are of type `MatrixVectorView`. Instances of this class hold a reference to the original matrix. Therefore, serializing an instance of `MatrixVectorView` effectively boils down to serializing the complete input matrix for each row. This means that the `CollectionInputFormat` needs memory of order `size(inputMatrix) * rows(inputMatrix)` to serialize the given collection of `DrmTuple &#91;Int&#93; ` instances. \\n\\n     The input size for the dals test case are `500 * 500`. This means that the input matrix has roughly the size of 2 MB. The serialized `CollectionInputFormat` has then a size of roughly 1 GB, because we serialize the matrix for each row. If you replace `FlinkEngine.scala:231` with `val rows = (0 until m.nrow).map(i =&gt; (i, dvec(m(i, : ).asInstanceOf &#91;Vector&#93; ))`, the test will pass the serialization point (but fail with another error   The reason why 1 GB of memory, given that you set the max limit to 4 GB, is already enough to crash Flink is that Flink reserver per default 70% of the available memory for its managed memory (for sorting and hashing). \\n\\n     I think it would make sense to convert possible `Views` to its materialized form before distributing the data in the cluster. That way, you avoid the creation of unnecessary data which might be ok for the local use case where the data is shared. \\n\\n     I hope this sheds a little bit of light in the `OutOfMemoryError` you\'ve encountered.               \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14967623_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'21\\/Oct\\/15 18:35\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-10-21T18:35:22+0000\'\u003e21\\/Oct\\/15 18:35\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eGithub user dlyubimov commented on the pull request:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/161#issuecomment-149987779\\\" class=\\\"external-link\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\u003ehttps:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/161#issuecomment-149987779\u003c\\/a\u003e\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    On Wed, Oct 21, 2015 at 5:48 AM, Till Rohrmann &lt;notifications@github.com&gt;\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    wrote:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    &gt; The problem of the OutOfMemoryError in dals of the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; DistributedDecompositionSuite is the following:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt;\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; In order parallelize the input matrix, the FlinkEngine creates a\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; Collection[DrmTuple\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;Int&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e] which is given to Flink\'s CollectionInputFormat.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; The CollectionInputFormat is simply a wrapper for a collection which is\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; serialized and shipped to the corresponding data source at runtime. The\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; problem is that the matrix rows in the collection of DrmTuple\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;Int&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e are of\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; type MatrixVectorView. Instances of this class hold a reference to the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; original matrix. Therefore, serializing an instance of MatrixVectorView\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; effectively boils down to serializing the complete input matrix for each\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; row.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt;\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    This has never been a problem for other mappings and should not be here.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    What you serialize is either (1) collection of vectors, or (2) a matrix\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    view.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    Java serialization of the mahout-math is not supported. so it has to be a\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    custom serialization in each case. Mahout core provides two serialization\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    means: (1) hadoop writable, (2) kryo.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    in particular, spark backend uses kryo serialization.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    In this case i guess we are speaking of collection of vectors, so the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    classes supprting these types of serialization would be VectorWritable and\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    \u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;1&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e. Kryo is generally a preferred way. We can move kryo support into\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    math-scala out of spark package if needed.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    if neither kryo nor writable fits the bill, then additional thought is\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    required. I remember vaguely talking to Stephan and he told me that\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    supporting Writable serialization will suffice as a minimum requirement. So\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    serializing vectors with either of these two ways should be acceptable\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    regardless of actual implementation (view\\/non-view, doesn\'t matter. they\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    serialize any Vector implementation).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    \u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;1&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/blob\\/master\\/spark\\/src\\/main\\/scala\\/org\\/apache\\/mahout\\/sparkbindings\\/io\\/VectorKryoSerializer.scala\\\" class=\\\"external-link\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\u003ehttps:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/blob\\/master\\/spark\\/src\\/main\\/scala\\/org\\/apache\\/mahout\\/sparkbindings\\/io\\/VectorKryoSerializer.scala\u003c\\/a\u003e\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e    &gt; This means that the CollectionInputFormat needs memory of order size(inputMatrix)\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; * rows(inputMatrix) to serialize the given collection of DrmTuple\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;Int&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; instances.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt;\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; The input size for the dals test case are 500 * 500. This means that the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; input matrix has roughly the size of 2 MB. The serialized\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; CollectionInputFormat has then a size of roughly 1 GB, because we\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; serialize the matrix for each row. If you replace FlinkEngine.scala:231\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; with val rows = (0 until m.nrow).map(i =&gt; (i, dvec(m(i,\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; :\u003cimg class=\\\"emoticon\\\" src=\\\"\\/jira\\/images\\/icons\\/emoticons\\/smile.png\\\" height=\\\"16\\\" width=\\\"16\\\" align=\\\"absmiddle\\\" alt=\\\"\\\" border=\\\"0\\\"\\/\u003e).asInstanceOf\u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;Vector&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e)), the test will pass the serialization point\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; (but fail with another error \u003cimg class=\\\"emoticon\\\" src=\\\"\\/jira\\/images\\/icons\\/emoticons\\/sad.png\\\" height=\\\"16\\\" width=\\\"16\\\" align=\\\"absmiddle\\\" alt=\\\"\\\" border=\\\"0\\\"\\/\u003e The reason why 1 GB of memory, given that\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; you set the max limit to 4 GB, is already enough to crash Flink is that\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; Flink reserver per default 70% of the available memory for its managed\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; memory (for sorting and hashing).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt;\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; I think it would make sense to convert possible Views to its materialized\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; form before distributing the data in the cluster. That way, you avoid the\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; creation of unnecessary data which might be ok for the local use case where\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; the data is shared.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt;\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; I hope this sheds a little bit of light in the OutOfMemoryError you\'ve\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; encountered.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt;\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; \\u2014\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n    &gt; \\n    wrote: \\n\\n     &gt; The problem of the OutOfMemoryError in dals of the \\n    &gt; DistributedDecompositionSuite is the following: \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; In order parallelize the input matrix, the FlinkEngine creates a \\n    &gt; Collection[DrmTuple &#91;Int&#93; ] which is given to Flink\'s CollectionInputFormat. \\n    &gt; The CollectionInputFormat is simply a wrapper for a collection which is \\n    &gt; serialized and shipped to the corresponding data source at runtime. The \\n    &gt; problem is that the matrix rows in the collection of DrmTuple &#91;Int&#93;  are of \\n    &gt; type MatrixVectorView. Instances of this class hold a reference to the \\n    &gt; original matrix. Therefore, serializing an instance of MatrixVectorView \\n    &gt; effectively boils down to serializing the complete input matrix for each \\n    &gt; row. \\n    &gt; \\n    This has never been a problem for other mappings and should not be here. \\n    What you serialize is either (1) collection of vectors, or (2) a matrix \\n    view. \\n\\n     Java serialization of the mahout-math is not supported. so it has to be a \\n    custom serialization in each case. Mahout core provides two serialization \\n    means: (1) hadoop writable, (2) kryo. \\n\\n     in particular, spark backend uses kryo serialization. \\n\\n     In this case i guess we are speaking of collection of vectors, so the \\n    classes supprting these types of serialization would be VectorWritable and \\n     &#91;1&#93; . Kryo is generally a preferred way. We can move kryo support into \\n    math-scala out of spark package if needed. \\n\\n     if neither kryo nor writable fits the bill, then additional thought is \\n    required. I remember vaguely talking to Stephan and he told me that \\n    supporting Writable serialization will suffice as a minimum requirement. So \\n    serializing vectors with either of these two ways should be acceptable \\n    regardless of actual implementation (view\\/non-view, doesn\'t matter. they \\n    serialize any Vector implementation). \\n\\n      &#91;1&#93;  \\n     https:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/blob\\/master\\/spark\\/src\\/main\\/scala\\/org\\/apache\\/mahout\\/sparkbindings\\/io\\/VectorKryoSerializer.scala  \\n\\n     &gt; This means that the CollectionInputFormat needs memory of order size(inputMatrix) \\n    &gt; * rows(inputMatrix) to serialize the given collection of DrmTuple &#91;Int&#93;  \\n    &gt; instances. \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; The input size for the dals test case are 500 * 500. This means that the \\n    &gt; input matrix has roughly the size of 2 MB. The serialized \\n    &gt; CollectionInputFormat has then a size of roughly 1 GB, because we \\n    &gt; serialize the matrix for each row. If you replace FlinkEngine.scala:231 \\n    &gt; with val rows = (0 until m.nrow).map(i =&gt; (i, dvec(m(i, \\n    &gt; : ).asInstanceOf &#91;Vector&#93; )), the test will pass the serialization point \\n    &gt; (but fail with another error   The reason why 1 GB of memory, given that \\n    &gt; you set the max limit to 4 GB, is already enough to crash Flink is that \\n    &gt; Flink reserver per default 70% of the available memory for its managed \\n    &gt; memory (for sorting and hashing). \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; I think it would make sense to convert possible Views to its materialized \\n    &gt; form before distributing the data in the cluster. That way, you avoid the \\n    &gt; creation of unnecessary data which might be ok for the local use case where \\n    &gt; the data is shared. \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; I hope this sheds a little bit of light in the OutOfMemoryError you\'ve \\n    &gt; encountered. \\n    &gt; \\n    &gt; \\u2014 \\n    &gt; Reply to this email directly or view it on GitHub \\n    &gt; &lt; https:\\/\\/github.com\\/apache\\/mahout\\/pull\\/161#issuecomment-149884474 &gt;. \\n    &gt; \\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n Flink\'s type extractor detects that this type is not a POJO and thus assigns it a `GenericTypeInfo`. Types with this type info are serialized using Kryo. Since kryo has no special serializer registered it will use the default one. The default serializer in this case is the `FieldSerializer`.
